Public Telegrams

Telegram from the Shandong Provincial Party Affairs Consolidation Committee

To all newspaper offices, please take note: It is reported that Korean farmers at Wanbaoshan forcibly reclaimed paddy fields, causing conflicts with our Chinese people. The Japanese government even dispatched garrison troops and police to massacre our Chinese people. This is an open and violent act of aggression that has been recognized by the world. All of our people are filled with indignation. Wherever our compatriots in Incheon, Pyongyang, and other places in Korea have set foot, Japanese imperialists have instigated Korean people to carry out cruel and brutal anti-Chinese movements. Nearly ten days have passed, and the matter has not yet ended. The harm and losses to the lives and property of our compatriots cannot be counted. This is unprecedented in any country without laws or order. Moreover, under the strict police rule of Japan in Korea, there is no doubt that this is an exposure of the Japanese government's planned and organized policy of aggression against China. If this can be tolerated, what kind of nation are we? International justice will be destroyed in the world. With the responsibility of national survival and the hatred of the enemy, in addition to directly telegraphing the Central Government, we have requested that a strong protest be lodged immediately, that the rioters be severely punished, that the affected compatriots be compensated, that all losses be compensated, and that it be guaranteed that the same incident will not happen again. We also ask that all effective methods of protecting overseas Chinese be implemented immediately. We hereby send this telegram for your information, hoping that comrades from all regions and compatriots from all over the country will rise up together and vow to fight to the death to uphold justice and safeguard national rights. We eagerly await your response and are filled with intense grief and anger. Sincerely, the Shandong Provincial Party Affairs Consolidation Committee.

Telegram from the Hebei Provincial Party Affairs Consolidation Committee

To all ministries, courts, and councils of the Nanjing National Government, all levels of party headquarters, all levels of government, and all newspaper offices, please take note: Recently, we sent a telegram to the Central Party Headquarters, which stated: "To the Nanjing Central Executive Committee: Urgently, in the Wanbaoshan area of Changchun County, Jilin, Korean residents, under the instigation of the Japanese, arbitrarily dug ditches and built dams that were seven or eight zhang wide and more than twenty li long, destroying more than a hundred xiang of our fertile farmland for no reason. The local farmers believe that the land belongs to us, and if the ditch is dug, the river water will overflow, and thousands of xiang of farmland along the ditch will be flooded. Moreover, the waterway in this area is a convenient channel, and if the dam is built, transportation will be cut off for hundreds of households along the river, and the residents will have no livelihood. Because this concerns their lives and families, there is no way to save themselves but to fight to the death. After repeated negotiations, the Japanese had other intentions and were arrogant and unreasonable. Not only did they not talk about reason and law, but they also sent armed police to assist in digging and building. The turmoil was expanded by the Japanese, and Foreign Minister Shidehara issued a telegram expressing protest and hinting at a second Jinan Incident. In recent days, the situation has become increasingly urgent. The Japanese have already fired thirty or more shots, killing more than a dozen of our farmers. The signs of disaster have already appeared. If such misery and persecution can still be tolerated, what is a nation? The Japanese have been operating in the Eastern Provinces for a long time and have been planning and plotting for a long time. They regard the Eastern Provinces as something in their pocket, which is now completely exposed. If a comprehensive countermeasure is not urgently determined, the future will be unimaginable. For this reason, we submit this telegram earnestly, earnestly urging the National Government to strictly supervise the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, lodge the most serious protest, and thoroughly plan comprehensive countermeasures. We send this telegram with sadness and anger, and cannot bear our urgency. May you unite and rise up to save the nation together. Most sincerely, the Hebei Provincial Party Affairs Consolidation Committee."

Special Commentary

A Review and Prospect of the Pacific International Academic Society (III) (Continued) Bin

(3) The Importance of the Third Conference

The Third Conference in the autumn of 1929 was held in Nara, Kyoto, Japan. The significance of this conference was the heated and serious discussion of the "Three Eastern Provinces Problem," which is related to the peace of East Asia and the world. In this heated and serious discussion, the representatives of our country made every effort to argue and debate, elaborating on the fact that unequal treaties had caused persecution in our country, and pointing out the Japanese conspiracy to annex our Northeast. This allowed representatives from various countries to have a considerable understanding of the current situation in this New China. The actual situation of Japan's aggression against our Northeast was also exposed to the world. The outline of the Third Conference is listed as follows.

(1) Outline of the Third Conference

Date: October 28 to November 9, 1929

Participating Countries: Australia, Britain, Canada, China, Japan, New Ceylon, the United States, etc.

List of Chinese Representatives

Zhou Tianfang, Wang Ziwen, Yan Baohang, Su Shangda, Ning Encheng, Wang Huibo, Dong Qizheng, Nan Bingfang, Tao Menghe, Cao Yanshen, Xu Shushi, Bao Mingqian, Chen Hengzhe, Wu Daquan, Zhang Boling, He Lian, Xu Baoqian, Zeng Baosun, Gui Zhiliang, Wu Yifang, Liu Dajun, Li Yinglin, Xia Jinlin, Pan Guangdan, Wen Peishan, Zeng Rongpu, Dai Airu, Chen Liting, Yu Rizhang, Wang Shijing

Important Issues

(1) The relationship between mechanical civilization and traditional culture (2) Industrialization problems (3) Population and food problems (4) Transportation problems (5) Pacific diplomatic relations problems (6) Foreign investment problems (7) The Three Eastern Provinces Problem (8) Chinese diplomatic problems

Page 8

It can be seen that half of the eight issues of this conference were Chinese issues, and the others were academic discussions. Moreover, the issues related to China are all practical issues that should be actively resolved at present. Therefore, in the conference agenda, the discussion of Chinese issues occupied nearly half of the conference time. The consular jurisdiction and concession issues are obviously unreasonable, unequal, and detrimental to our country's sovereignty. Moreover, foreign nationals from Russia, Germany, Austria, and other countries can live and work in China in peace under the protection of legal rights. After the recovery of the Hankou and Xunyang concessions, the foreign nationals in the two places were also very peaceful. This further demonstrates that there is no reason to continue to retain consular jurisdiction and concessions. However, the representatives of the Pacific Conference countries, who were standing on the position of people's diplomacy, unanimously advocated postponing the handling of the issues. The discussion of the Three Eastern Provinces Problem continued for three days. The Japanese representatives consistently maintained a stubborn attitude consistent with their government and engaged in unreasonable debates, acting as spokespersons for their government. They even said that it was their country's legitimate right to invade our Northeast, and that our country's opposition to invasion was a crime against justice. Their tyrannical and unreasonable attitude fundamentally deviated from the position of people's diplomacy. As a result, the achievements of this conference failed to have a good impact on the future of national relations in the Pacific. The original intention and spirit of convening the conference were therefore in vain. This is what we deeply regret.

Important News

Detailed Record of the Wanbaoshan Incident in Changchun

Inspection of Majiashaokou

Harbin Correspondence: The case of Korean farmers planting rice in Wanbaoshan, Changchun, which shocked the country, became an important diplomatic case after the conflict on July 2. Japanese newspapers promoted and exaggerated it and made unreasonable records. I went to Changchun on the evening of the 4th to investigate the truth and went to Majiashao, the scene of the incident, and obtained the following results.

Truth of the Second Day Incident

In May of this year, the Wanbao Mountain incident occurred, becoming entangled and unresolved. The farmers repeatedly urged the government to resolve it, but the Japanese consul-general always used the excuse of maintaining the vested interests of Koreans to refuse to stop the trench-digging work. Recently, the trenches have become several *zhang* (丈, ~3 meters) deep and twenty *li* (里, ~0.5 km) long. The dam construction at Majia Sentinel Post was successful, and water had already begun to flow into the newly dug trenches. The Japanese consulate-general intensified its work, urging the Koreans to complete it by the end of June. Due to the damming of the Yitong River downstream, the upstream water level deepened daily, reaching within a foot of overflowing the banks. The farmers, already pained by the digging on their good farmland, feared that their crops would be flooded. Farmers from two or three districts with vested interests, led by village chiefs, decided on June 30th that on the morning of July 1st, each household would send one able-bodied man to gather at Yaowo Fort to automatically fill the drainage ditches. On that day, they also slaughtered a pig and smeared blood, jointly swearing an oath to resist the Japanese police to the end. On the morning of July 1st at 6:00 AM, farmers from dozens of villages in the Wanbao Mountain area gathered at Yaowo Fort, totaling over 700 people. Each carried hoes and shovels, led by representatives Qu Xianglou and Sun Rongqing, bearing large banners of white cloth inscribed in red characters on all four sides, reading: "The cultivated land related to the lives and livelihoods of us all has been cut in two by illegally dug ditches, harming everyone's work. We have repeatedly petitioned the government, but to no avail. Forced to do so, we have decided to take matters into our own hands and implement legitimate self-defense measures, on the one hand, restoring the original state for cultivation, and on the other hand, requesting the government to order the illegal persons to compensate for the damages. This is a public declaration to make known to all. Announced by the victims of the Wanbao Mountain farmland." At approximately 7:00 AM, they arrived at the bank of the Yitong River at the former Majia Sentinel Post. The Koreans were still building the dam, and there were six Japanese police officers at the scene monitoring. After the farmers arrived, they planted the banners on the ground and immediately began filling the ditches and destroying the dam in sections. Fifteen *li* of ditches were filled, and the dam was completely destroyed. At that time, the Japanese police officers stepped forward to block them, questioning their reasons. The farmer representatives replied that they were filling the ditches to facilitate cultivation and were not there to cause a fight. The Japanese police officers, finding themselves in the wrong, were at a loss for words. One of them suddenly grabbed the representative's sleeve and butted him in the head. Another lay down in the ditch, acting like a rogue. However, the farmers continued their work. By 12:00 PM, the ditch had been filled, and the farmers lined up and left. Before leaving, the Japanese police officers asked if they would come again tomorrow. The representatives replied that they would still come. When asked how many people would come, they replied, "Today 700, tomorrow 1,000." The Japanese police officers angrily said that if 1,000 came tomorrow, they should bring 1,000 coffins. "My empire will dispatch troops tonight. Airplanes, cannons, machine guns, and bombs are all ready. If 1,000 come, 1,000 will die, not a single one will return alive." After the farmers left, the Japanese police officers immediately sent a message by carrier pigeon to the Japanese consulate-general, urgently requesting reinforcements. On the morning of the 2nd, 30 Japanese police officers arrived, carrying rifles, pistols, and a large quantity of ammunition, led by the chief of the Japanese police station, Nakagawa Yoshiharu. They dispersed to the left and right of the drainage ditch. At approximately 8:00 AM, farmers from various villages were still gathering, carrying hoes. They arrived at Majia Sentinel Post. The Japanese police chief, Nakagawa, led armed police to block them head-on, seeking to speak with representatives. More than ten people, including Sun Rongqing and Qu Xianglou, came forward. Nakagawa asked why they were filling the dam and when they would stop this movement. Sun and others replied as before, stating that they would stop the movement when the original state was restored. Seeing that Sun and others' replies were very firm, Nakagawa's expression suddenly changed. He shouted, ordering the Japanese police to tie up Sun Rongqing. Four or five Japanese police officers dragged Sun away, pulling him toward the tent. The general farmers, seeing this, were greatly angered and swarmed forward, surrounding the Japanese police and snatching Sun back. At this time, the Japanese police opened fire, firing into the air as a warning. The farmers were in an uproar, retreating about a *li*. More than a hundred of them, whose homes were closer, ran back to retrieve guns, using the He family's house walls at the former Majia Sentinel Post as cover, returning fire. They held their ground for a while, but there were no casualties. At that time, the chief of the third branch of the county public security bureau, Tian Xigu, upon hearing the news, rushed to the scene with police, braving the rain of bullets to mediate with the farmers, persuading them to stop firing. Some of the farmers, excessively angered, actually struck Tian, breaking Tian's left shoulder with a steel hoe. However, Tian still endured the pain and tried his best to dissuade them. The farmers were slightly moved and stopped firing. On the Japanese police side, Tian also risked going to persuade them to stop. By 10:00 AM, the main body of farmers was still retreating. This was the actual situation of the conflict on July 2nd.

Japanese Police Dig Trenches to Prepare for War

After the conflict on the 2nd, the Japanese consulate-general received the report and continuously dispatched armed police to the scene. They also transported two light machine guns, one handheld machine gun, and dozens of boxes of ammunition by large carts, all under the command of Nakagawa Yoshiharu, for military deployment. They immediately built a trench two *li* long within the filled drainage ditch, turning the earth into a trench. They set up machine guns facing the Majia Sentinel Post village. At night, they placed one sentry with a rifle every few tens of paces. During the day, they used carrier pigeons to report the situation to the consulate-general. As of the 5th, the number of Japanese police had increased to 73. In addition to setting up one or two tents and sleeping in the open near the dam, a part of them, about 20 or so, led by Nakagawa, invaded the residence of Wang, a farmer in the former Majia Sentinel Post, driving out Wang's entire family of over 20 people and occupying his main house. Wang's family members all moved elsewhere. Only the head of the household and his brother requested permission from the Japanese side to remain in the house to take care of everything, but they had to perform odd jobs for the Japanese police every day. The He family's residence on the left was also invaded and occupied by Koreans. The women and able-bodied men all moved to other places, with only a few elderly and weak people remaining in the house. In the nearby farming villages, due to the Japanese police's strict preparations, the elderly, young, and women all moved to distant places in advance, with each household guarded by able-bodied men. Since the 2nd, the road to the section of Jianbao-Qian Majia Sentinel Post, spanning ten *li*, was devoid of travelers. All the actions of the Japanese police were spied on by the farmers and reported to the representatives of each village twice a day. At the Majia Sentinel Post on the Yitong River, there was originally a ferry operated by farmers, dedicated to ferrying villagers back and forth on the east and west banks. Each year, each village contributed a certain amount of money to it. The operator had been in the business for 30 years, relying on it for his family's livelihood. After July 2nd, he was driven out by the Japanese police, who seized the ferry. Traffic on both sides was thus cut off. More than 70 Korean able-bodied men, under the supervision of the Japanese police, were actively building dikes to block the water, fearing that the farmers would come again to destroy them. They changed to using willow branches interspersed with sand and soil, stacked together and surrounded by wooden stakes, making them extremely solid. All the willows on both banks of the Yitong River, both upstream and downstream, were cut down completely for construction materials. However, the Koreans were beaten and scolded if they worked even slightly slowly. Those who feared hardship took the opportunity to escape. Originally, there were 188 men, women, old, and young. Currently, apart from the 72 able-bodied men working at the Majia Sentinel Post, the women, old, and young are living near the Wanbao Mountain farm. Furthermore, farmers in each village, because the Japanese side's dike-building work did not stop, and the upstream water level increased daily, feared that if there was heavy rain in the coming days, four or five thousand *qing* (頃, ~6.67 hectares) of fields along the banks would be flooded. Therefore, they were extremely indignant and spontaneously established the Wanbao Mountain Farmers' Foreign Affairs Support Association. Each household contributed at least one able-bodied man, forming a united village association, electing four directors and 30 executive members to confront the Japanese and requesting the government to take charge as soon as possible. On one hand, they sent people to spy on the actions of the Japanese police. If the Korean people continued to dig drainage ditches within the day, or the Yitong River flooded due to the construction of the dike, the farmers would inevitably fight the Japanese police. The Japanese police had already heard this news and specially buried landmines on both sides of the drainage ditch. Therefore, the current situation is still extremely dangerous.

Inspecting Majia Sentinel Post

I arrived in Changchun at 7:30 AM on the 5th. After visiting the county government, public security bureau, county farmers' association, and municipal preparatory office and obtaining detailed information, and considering that Majia Sentinel Post was the site of the Sino-Japanese conflict, I specially requested the municipal office to send someone to guide me there. In addition to notifying the Japanese consulate-general, the municipal office sent three people to accompany me: translator Zhou Wuxiang, and guards Zhang Wanchun and Li Chengye. At 6:30 AM on the morning of the 6th, led by village representatives Qu Xianglou and Sun Jiayuan, we set off on horseback. At approximately 9:00 AM, we passed the upper reaches of the Yitong River. The place was 18 *li* away from the Majia Sentinel Post, where the dike was being built. However, the water was already high, and the river had widened. The place where the water was usually shallow enough for vehicles and horses to wade through was no longer passable. The group stopped their horses on the riverbank, hesitating for a long time, with no way to pass. Finally, they risked whipping their horses across, but the water was already above the horses' bellies, and the entire group's clothing was soaked. After crossing the river, we encountered farmers along the way reporting on the situation at Majia Sentinel Post in an endless stream. At noon, we rested at Qu Xianglou's house in Jianbao, and the people and horses had a light meal. At 12:10 PM in the afternoon, we continued forward, passing Cun Jin Fort. We were close to Majia Sentinel Post, and there were fewer and fewer pedestrians. Finally, at 1:50 PM in the afternoon, we arrived at the rear Majia Sentinel Post. From horseback, we could see the Japanese police in yellow uniforms, going back and forth, appearing very busy. The group stopped at the residence of Wang Jia San, a farmer. A farmer held a note and went forward. The reporter and Zhou Wuxiang followed behind, walking to the Japanese police station at Majia Sentinel Post. The farmer handed the note to the Japanese police officer residing in Wang's farmhouse. After Nakagawa Yoshiharu inspected it, he made no expression. The reporter then went straight in. At that time, Nakagawa and Takahashi Hiroki of the Japanese consulate-general were sitting on the *kang* (炕, heated brick bed). Seeing the reporter come in, they jumped down and shook hands. After exchanging pleasantries, the reporter stated that news reporters have no international views and that he had come purely to investigate the truth. At this point, Nakagawa immediately stated his mission in the area without being asked, which was translated by Takahashi Hiroki. The general idea was that on July 1st, Chinese farmers gathered in large numbers to fill the dike and destroy the ditch, almost causing a conflict with the Koreans. He had been ordered by the consul to lead the police to protect the work of the Korean people. On the morning of the 2nd, Chinese farmers came again. They were deeply afraid of rioting because they were raising banners and shouting. He had also seen Sun Rongqing carrying a handgun, so he had dragged him to confiscate his weapon. Other farmers opened fire at the Japanese police as a warning. The Japanese police also fired into the air. Later, they were persuaded by the branch bureau chief to stop firing. There were no deaths or injuries on either side. This was an extremely small problem, and they sincerely hoped it could be resolved satisfactorily as soon as possible so that they could return to Changchun. They were currently living in this house because the owner had voluntarily invited them. The daily needs they consumed were all brought by themselves and did not cost the owner a cent. They would also need the consul's order to withdraw in the future. Takahashi Hiroki also said that there were a total of 47 Japanese police officers. Although the ferry had been taken over by the Japanese police, the original owner was given 200 *diao* (吊, string of cash coins) per day (six *jiao* [角, ~0.1 yuan] in Shanghai silver dollars) as compensation. Because the dike prevented ships from traveling directly upstream and downstream, goods could be transferred between them, and any losses would be compensated by the Japanese. 45 *mu* (畝, ~0.067 hectares) of rice fields had already been planted in Wanbao Mountain. A total of 120 Koreans, several of whom had been deported by the Chinese police. While he was speaking, three farmers from the house came into the room to retrieve items and were scolded out by Takahashi. The reporter could not help but feel a pang of sadness. During the conversation, Nakagawa ordered the Japanese police to bring beer and soda to show goodwill. He opened a bottle and repeatedly urged the others to drink, and they each drank a glass. Afterwards, at the reporter's request, they went to inspect the drainage ditch and dam. Nakagawa agreed, and Takahashi led the way. The dam was about a *li* away from Wang's farmhouse. The water had already been forced back, with a difference of nearly five *chi* (尺, ~0.3 meters) in water level between the upstream and downstream. The dike was over 1 *zhang* high, 7 *chi* wide, and 3 *zhang* long. Both ends had been completed, with only the middle not yet finished. Dozens of Koreans were cutting willow branches and tying them with hemp rope, and using hemp sacks to fill with soil and pile on the dike. It could be completed in a few more days. However, although the water level had risen, it was still far from the entrance of the drainage ditch. The drainage ditch was 8 *chi* deep but had been leveled by the farmers and had not yet been dug through. Even if it were dug through, it would still need to be deepened to 1.5 or 2 *zhang*. Therefore, this clumsy project could be said to be unwise. The filled drainage ditch was shaped into a trench, winding for two *li*. Three Japanese police tents were set up next to the ditch. Many Japanese soldiers were resting inside, glaring at the reporter with fierce eyes and hastily covering the machine guns with the tents. The reporter took several photos. At that time, a Japanese police officer secretly reported to Nakagawa that he should stop it. Nakagawa, because the reporter had obtained his permission in advance, was unable to go back on his word and shook his head to indicate that it was not possible. However, he told the reporter not to exaggerate the report after returning, so as not to lose the truth. After standing by the dam for a long time, they returned to Majia Sentinel Post. The general farmers, at first thinking that the group's trip would be dangerous, were all worried. When they saw them return safely, they all offered their congratulations. At approximately 3:00 PM, they departed from Majia Sentinel Post to return to the city. On the way, they encountered a rainstorm and took shelter at the Li family's farmhouse in Jianbao. They resumed their journey at 4:00 PM, and upon reaching the original ferry crossing on the Yitong River, the water level was too high to cross again. They urged their horses several *li* away and crossed under the Jiang Bridge. They did not return to the city until 9:00 PM. Wanbao Mountain had no Japanese police stationed there and was not currently a tense location, so they stopped going there. (July 8th)

Korean Anti-Chinese Sentiment Spreads to Japan

Overseas Chinese in Osaka and Kanazawa Beaten

All Utensils and Objects Were Damaged

Osaka Dispatch: The Koreans' savage nature of abusing and killing overseas Chinese has gradually spread to the entire territory of Japan. Reports of Korean people destroying overseas Chinese residences and beating overseas Chinese have been heard daily. Such incidents have occurred in Osaka, Kanazawa, and Kobe. Although the Japanese local governments have expressed their utmost protection of overseas Chinese, they have turned a blind eye to the actions of the Korean people. Therefore, on the night of the 7th of this month, two barbershops run by overseas Chinese in the Kanazawa area, near Osaka Prefecture, were broken into by 23 Korean people from the surrounding area, each carrying weapons such as sticks and clubs. The overseas Chinese families, due to their lack of resistance, had 11 people beaten, with two severely injured and their lives in danger. The rioters also completely destroyed the houses and utensils. On the morning of the 8th, Zhou Jue, the consul in Kobe, rushed to inspect the damage and immediately protested to the Osaka local authorities. Also, at 11:00 PM on the night of the 8th, the home of Zhang Guoshun, an overseas Chinese residing in Zhuangzhong Street, Higashiyodogawa Ward, Osaka, was also broken into by more than a dozen Korean people, who smashed the doors and windows with stones and used sticks to beat Zhang to the ground. The utensils were completely damaged, and property was looted. Zhang was seriously injured and unconscious and was later taken to a nearby hospital for treatment. It is said that his life is in danger. By the time the police arrived, the rioters had fled without a trace. Korean people also repeatedly beat Chinese people on the streets. In fact, the Japanese are unable to protect overseas Chinese. There are no fewer than 300,000 Korean people currently residing in the Japanese mainland. The massacre of Chinese people could easily erupt. If the national government does not quickly find a way to effectively protect overseas Chinese, the overseas Chinese in Japan may suffer the same tragic fate as the overseas Chinese in Korea. (July 9th)

Korean Riots Affect Andong

Escaped Overseas Chinese Describe the Tragic Situation of Compatriots in Korea

More Than 2,000 People Fled to Andong Alone

One Tattered Korean Garment Costs 300 Yen in Japanese Currency

The Japanese Side Verbally Agreed to Stop It, But It Was Still Ineffective

The Turmoil Extended to Sinuiju, Alarming Andong

The Chinese Consulate in Sinuiju Was Smashed by Korean People

Currently, All Sectors Have Begun to Raise Relief Funds for the Refugees

Andong Special Dispatch: In the Korean interior, unemployed Korean people have been entering the country as laborers, earning low wages and working diligently, causing resentment among the Chinese workers who fear being deprived of their livelihoods. They had long planned to expel them from the country, but had not had the opportunity until now. This time, the Wanbao Mountain incident spread from afar. A general group of malcontents used it as an excuse, instigating each other from all sides. The Japanese also deliberately fabricated rumors, exaggerating the matter. The fuse for the massacre of Chinese people was thus ignited, and it could not be contained. The bloody tragedy spread throughout Korea. On the 6th and 7th, the trains coming from Korea were filled with no fewer than 2,000 overseas Chinese fleeing for refuge, their hair disheveled and faces covered in dirt, a pitiful sight. According to the returning overseas Chinese, a tragic massacre suddenly occurred in the Seoul, Incheon, Pyongyang, and Seoncheon areas on the afternoon of the 3rd. Korean rioters formed gangs, their momentum very fierce. They searched the homes of overseas Chinese and killed them at will. They first set fire to and destroyed their goods, knocked down their houses, and then killed people and divided the property. Countless overseas Chinese died, but the exact number is unknown. The rioters then used automobiles at night to transport the bodies and throw them into the river, destroying the evidence. Their designs were also cunning. When the tragedy was first discovered, the consul-general in Seoul, Zhang Weicheng, and the chairman of the Chinese Chamber of Commerce rushed to see the director of the police bureau and the head of the foreign affairs section of the Governor-General's Office, requesting them to quickly stop the rioters' rampages and protect the overseas Chinese. The Japanese authorities verbally agreed completely, but it has not been effective. The rioters continue to rampage as before, still massacring and looting. At that time, a Shanghai merchant named Wu planned to establish a branch in Seoncheon and had shipped textiles worth 50,000 Shanghai silver dollars from Shanghai. Unexpectedly, when the goods arrived in Seoul, it coincided with the opening of the tragedy. All the goods were divided up by the rioters. Wu committed suicide upon hearing the news. Near Namdaemun in Seoul, the Guo family of eight people, barbers from Hubei, were all killed at the same time, with no one spared. On the morning of the 6th, Consul Zhang saw that the situation was serious and could not be stopped. He protected the Chinese and got them on the train to flee back to Andong. At this time, the overseas Chinese who had taken refuge in the consulate were crowded together. The rioters rushed in, smashing everything they saw, and the Chinese Chamber of Commerce was also affected. At this time, the situation was urgent, and each station stopped selling train tickets to overseas Chinese. The overseas Chinese there were even more panicked, and many wanted to return but could not. Therefore, they had no choice but to buy Korean clothes at high prices, posing as Korean people, buy tickets, get on the train, and hurriedly return home. Each short jacket actually cost more than 300 yen in Japanese currency. Unexpectedly, this evil trend spread quickly and extended to Sinuiju (separated from Andong by only a river). On the afternoon of the 6th, the Korean people there also suddenly rioted, seeking revenge on the Chinese and looting Chinese businesses. Although the Japanese police came out to stop them, they were ineffective. However, the overseas Chinese who were young and strong crossed the river overnight and were able to flee back to Andong, but they were empty-handed and abandoned all their property. The women, children, elderly, and weak remained there, their survival uncertain. The Chinese consul stationed in Sinuiju negotiated with the Japanese side, but to no avail, and fearing offending the rioters, there was no small danger. He also crossed the river to temporarily avoid the storm. On the morning of the 7th, overseas Chinese representatives Dou Yude and others went to various agencies to report the tragedy. At the same time, the people of the city, hot-blooded heroes, indignant at the injustice, wanted to retaliate against the Korean people in Andong, but were persuaded to stop by the authorities. The overseas Chinese in Andong felt uneasy and had disappeared from Chinese Street since the morning of the 7th. However, the air in Chinese Street in the city was tense, and there was a sense of impending crisis. It was heard that the Korean people in the Liudao Gou area were eager to try something, relying on something. Three or five cases of Korean people gathering to seek out and beat Chinese people had been discovered, but fortunately they were stopped in time and their desires were not fulfilled. On the afternoon of the 7th, the Chinese and Japanese police were on full alert, setting up checkpoints and increasing patrols along the streets, patrolling throughout the night to prevent Korean people from rioting. The Japanese police station informed the Chinese merchants and residents under its jurisdiction that they must close their doors before 8:00 PM in the evening, otherwise they would not be responsible for any other incidents that occurred. Wang Jiegong, the magistrate of Andong County, sent a telegram to the provincial officials on the morning of the 7th and negotiated with the Japanese consul, urging them to stop the Korean people from rioting as soon as possible. In addition, no fewer than 3,000 refugees from Korea and Sinuiju had fled, most of whom had no relatives to turn to and were sleeping on the streets, and there was a risk of starvation. Therefore, they joined forces with the Public Security Bureau and the Chamber of Commerce to find ways to provide relief, temporarily borrowing the Danggui and Xinming two stages and the Zhengyu Hao Sanhe Sheng oil mill in the city as shelters. All Chinese who had no relatives to rely on were accepted. As of the morning of the 8th, 1,200 refugees had been accommodated, and steamed buns were prepared as food. The expenses were temporarily advanced by the county government and the Chamber of Commerce. In addition, the county government, the Public Security Bureau, and the Chamber of Commerce each sent special personnel to take care of the refugees in the shelter. (July 8th)

Another dispatch states that after the tragedy was caused in Wanbao Mountain, District 3, Changchun, Jilin Province, by Japanese instigating Koreans to seize rice fields and forcibly dig ditches, the Koreans in various parts of Korea rose up in swarms, abusing our overseas compatriots, and actually developed into an unprecedented tragedy with blood flying everywhere. Reports have been pouring in from various places in recent days, making them unbearable to read. Unexpectedly, the entire Korean population of Sinuiju (Korean territory), across the river from Andong, also gathered a crowd on the evening of the 6th, marched in procession, and demonstrated in the streets. They beat any Chinese they encountered. By around 8:00 AM on the morning of the 7th, their actions were even more violent. Each held wooden sticks or large stones, and in an instant, the Donyufu, Taishengxiang, Yixingsheng, and Xinhua Yuan shops of Chinese merchants in Zhensha Town, Sinuiju, as well as the Dongshenglong shop of large Japanese merchants on Japanese Street, were all simultaneously struck by wood and stones. Windows and doors were broken, and much of the property inside was looted by the Koreans. Our overseas compatriots saw that the Japanese army's superficial efforts to stop them were ineffective, so they had no choice but to abandon their property and flee to Andong City. Our country's consulate in Sinuiju was also tragically smashed. As a result, the entire Chinese houses and property in Sinuiju suffered countless losses, totaling more than 300 Chinese merchants. From morning (7th) to 8:00 PM, approximately 3,000 overseas compatriots escaped, all filled with grievances and crying together. Those who had branches or relatives and friends in this city all came to take refuge. Those who had nowhere to turn were protected by the government, borrowed land for accommodation, and the Public Security Bureau provided porridge and rice to maintain their lives. From 9:00 AM to 9:00 PM, the first, second, and third bridges connecting this city and the Japanese concession temporarily increased guards from both China and Japan to prevent Koreans from traveling back and forth and causing conflicts. After 9:00 PM, traffic was cut off between the Chinese and Japanese borders. Our city temporarily increased the business community and patrolled along the streets to protect them. The atmosphere was tense throughout the city, and the situation was unusually turbulent. At approximately 1:00 PM, Zhang Hanwei, director of the business port public security bureau, and Wang Jiegong, the county magistrate, both went to the Danggui stage to comfort the returning overseas compatriots, urging them to wait for negotiations and promising to satisfy the affected compatriots. In the afternoon, the Japanese consul in this city visited our county government, but because the situation was unclear, negotiations could not begin. Chinese merchants in the concession all closed their doors at 9:00 PM in the evening. The night markets in the city and the concession were all temporarily suspended. In our city, Chinese merchants and residents residing in Korea were protected by our police to prevent accidents. (July 8th)

US Newspaper Commentary on the Wanpaoshan Incident

A Result of Japanese Conspiracy

Attempted Japanese Immigration Fails

Turning to Exploiting Korean Farmers

The World News Agency translates a review from the "Millard's Review" stating: The Japanese government's attempt to relocate its own people to Manchuria has failed, but they are not discouraged. They are now obviously trying to achieve the same goal by utilizing Koreans. Various incidents have occurred in the Eastern Provinces in recent months, especially the Wanpaoshan Incident, which is the most noteworthy. This is a direct result of the Japanese plan to use Koreans to immigrate to Manchuria. Initially, Japan planned to relocate Japanese people to Manchuria, but despite spending huge sums of money, it was ultimately unsuccessful. After twenty years of operation, the total number of Japanese people in Manchuria is no more than 200,000. Of these, 150,000 live in the Kwantung Leased Territory, the Japanese Concessions of Shenyang and Changchun, and the Japanese-controlled areas along the South Manchuria Railway. Most of these Japanese people are directly or indirectly related to the South Manchuria Railway's coal mining industry or various subsidiary businesses operated by the South Manchuria Railway. The independent Japanese colonization of Manchuria has completely failed because they cannot compete with the Chinese.

In view of the failure of relocating Japanese farmers to South Manchuria, the Japanese government turned its attention to Koreans. Initially, the Japanese government did not pay much attention to the Koreans' immigration to China, so there were few contacts with the Chinese authorities. Thousands of Koreans became Chinese citizens and lived peacefully with the millions of Chinese farmers who moved from Shandong to the Eastern Provinces. In recent years, however, the Japanese government, or at least the Japanese military cliques that controlled Japanese enterprises in South Manchuria, gradually paid attention to the Koreans, forcing them to register with the Japanese consulates, prohibiting them from paying taxes to the Chinese authorities, and encouraging them to resist any interference from the Chinese authorities. Whenever there was a dispute between Chinese and Koreans, the Japanese immediately sent troops to engage in "protection." If Koreans suffered any losses due to conflicts between China and Korea, the Japanese side would make compensation claims, which would create a tense situation with the potential to cause actual war.

The organization in charge of relocating Korean farmers to South Manchuria and Inner Mongolia is the Oriental Development Company. This company is formally subsidized by the Japanese government and was established in 1908 for the purpose of encouraging Japanese farmers to relocate to Korea. In recent years, the company has borrowed huge sums of money from the United States and France to subsidize the relocation of Korean farmers to South Manchuria. According to the Japan Yearbook, the Oriental Development Company has a capital of 50 million yen, and its bonds reach 141.1 million yen, which is three times its capital. The company provides loans to Korean farmers on generous terms or organizes Korean agricultural companies for terms ranging from five to twenty-five years. The Japanese government has approved the company's existence for 100 years. Its president and two vice presidents are appointed by the Japanese government and must be Japanese. Another vice president can be a Korean. All agricultural colonization areas established by the company are protected by the Japanese army and extraterritorial rights. Therefore, they are not under the jurisdiction of Chinese courts, nor do they pay taxes to the Chinese authorities. As the relocation areas of Koreans gradually increase, the Japanese General Staff also gradually increases its troops stationed in Chinese territory for protection.

Local Correspondence

Suzhou

Young Woman Abused and Commits Suicide by Swallowing Opium

Wang Luo, the wife of Wang Yekui, the young owner of the Tongdetai Military Oil Shop on Nanhai Street outside Changmen Gate, committed suicide by swallowing opium the other day due to unbearable beatings and abuse from her parents-in-law and husband. After the local court sent personnel to verify that there were indeed injuries, her husband, Wang Yekui, was escorted to the court by the Public Security Bureau for investigation and then detained. The mother and family of the deceased have now hired lawyer Xia to file a petition with the court requesting redress. Wang Yekui, on the other hand, has hired lawyers Sun and Jing, citing that many members of the deceased's family have occupied and disturbed the peace before the funeral arrangements, and has also filed a lawsuit with the court.

Losses from Continuous Heavy Rain

The continuous heavy rain has had a huge impact on rice seedlings in various townships. The shuttle boats that are usually relied upon for transportation have been suspended in eight or nine out of ten cases. Yesterday (the 12th), Qian Tianpeng, the director of the Construction Bureau, learned that the fields near Lake Taihu have been completely submerged. If it rains again, the district public offices in the towns and cities will also be submerged. The shuttle boats are docked at the Waitangqiao port and cannot pass the bridge to proceed further. Late rice is mainly grown in this area, and the rice seedlings have now been submerged in the water. In Guangfu, three or four out of ten of the rice fields at the Shanren Bridge in Hengjing have been submerged. The shuttle boats have been suspended, and the pond banks have been submerged by water. Wangjiaji in this township has become a swamp, and the houses have been completely submerged. More than 3,000 mu of fields in the 12th and 20th Tu of Huangdai have been completely submerged. The autumn harvest is estimated to be only 50% of what it could have been. Houses are flooded, and the water in the streets and alleys is ankle-deep. The pond banks along the river are submerged, and the shuttle boats are not running. Because Yishan, Guoxiang, and Xietang are attached to Suzhou City, the shuttle boats are still running, but the low-lying fields are completely submerged. The telephone lines in Lumu are blocked, and transportation is not possible. The river water in Mudu has risen by more than five feet in the past few days. The shuttle boat only ran one trip yesterday (the 12th). After the small boat from Dongshan City arrived at Shitang, passengers were ferried by small boats. The shuttle boat between that place and Hengjing has been suspended for three days.

Changshu

Various Things After Continuous Rain

Since entering the rainy season, there have been continuous rains in this county, especially the heavy rains on the 5th, 6th, and 7th, which were even more severe. The river water rose several feet sharply, and the low-lying rice seedlings were all submerged. As a result, the villagers were greatly panicked and reported to various businesses. The disaster situation was most severe in the areas of Dongtang City, Shipai, Renyang, Wuta, Nanhengjing, and Liantang. More than 20,000 mu of seedlings were washed away by the water. Ships can sail in the fields. In terms of transportation, the villagers in various places are building embankments to prevent water intrusion. However, the operation of shuttle boats is enough to damage the embankments, so the villagers prevent the shuttle boats from sailing. If anyone violates this, they will definitely attack them with huge stones and dirty feces. Therefore, the shuttle boats to and from various ports in this county have all stopped anchoring. As a result, news is isolated, and out-of-port postal correspondence arrives only after three days, and Shanghai newspapers must also be read once every three days, but they are delivered by special ships.

Commander Zhu Comes to Changshu to Interrogate the Major Bandit

The Second Battalion of the Pacification and Security Team stationed in Changshu previously arrested three major bandits, Wang Fengyi, Lu Rujin, and Chen Changwan, in Hupu. After several interrogations by the camp director, the three criminals were to be sent to the headquarters for review. Now, Supervisor Zhang telegraphed Regiment Commander and Commander Zhu Mian to come to Changshu from Suzhou to conduct on-site interrogation. Zhu arrived in Changshu on the 7th with Judge Advocate Zhu Shengwu and questioned the three bandits one by one at the battalion headquarters. Each bandit still confessed as before. Now Commander Zhu has decided to conduct a personal investigation in Changshu before proceeding with the review. If it is true, he will definitely execute them locally. On the 9th, Zhu hired a small motorboat and returned to Suzhou.

Wuxi

The Xiyi Section of the Ring Lake Road Will Soon Be Under Construction

After Sun Hongzhe, Director of the Construction Department, decided that the earth and stone works of the Xiyi section of the Ring Lake Provincial Highway would be contracted by Xiangtai and Xiehe Companies, the director of the local Construction Bureau ordered the department to rush to make the project contract. It has now been completed and is expected to start construction around the 20th. Director Sun of the Construction Department specially came to Wuxi with Deng Zaichen, Director of the Electrical Department, the other day. Yesterday morning, they went to Meiyuan, Yuantouzhu, Dushanmen and other places to inspect the Xiyi section of the Ring Lake Avenue. The inspection situation was that near Yuantouzhu and the opposite side of the Wuli Lake, a bridge was planned to be built at a narrow and shallow part of the lake, so that it could be used by Fangqiao and other places to drive around the lake. Director Deng of the Electrical Department plans to plant poles and hang lines along the Xiyi section of Taihu Lake to install telephones to facilitate the suppression of bandits along the lake and the communication of news on the Xiyi Road. After the inspection, they went to Taihu Hotel for a rest and decided to return to the province today.

Regulations on the Recruitment Area of the Military Police

The county government had previously repeatedly received instructions from the General Headquarters of the Army, Navy, and Air Force that recruitment by the military police should be prohibited in the provinces of Jiangsu, including Suzhou, Songjiang, Changshu, and Tai, and Zhejiang, including Hangzhou, Jiaxing, and Huzhou, but other areas could be handled accordingly. However, recently, Li Jinlan, a recruiter from the 5th Group of the Military Police Department, Zhou Rongchang, a recruitment branch committee member, and Zhao Ying, a conscripted student committee member from the 4th Division of the Army, came to Wuxi one after another to set up recruitment offices in temples and monasteries inside and outside the city, and successively sent letters to the Public Security Bureau requesting assistance. The county government had previously received orders to prohibit recruitment, and had not received any provincial orders this time, so it should prevent it as the opportunity arose, and immediately ordered the County Public Security Bureau to dissuade its subordinates in order to comply with the orders.

Changzhou

A Record of the Rain Disaster in Mengcheng

Menghe City in the western countryside of Wujin is flanked by mountains on the east and west, forming an embracing trend, so it is also known as Pearl City. There are many shops in the city, and famous doctors emerge in large numbers. Those who come from all over the provinces from afar to seek treatment are in an endless stream. The weather was very hot this month. On the 2nd and 3rd, there were thunderstorms, day and night. The mountain water on both sides rushed straight down, causing the South Water Gate of the city to be suddenly destroyed. The water was vast, truly like the scene of flooding Jinshan Temple. The villagers beat gongs and built ports, and were extremely panicked. The city was flooded to a depth of two or three feet. Shops and households were flooded and unable to trade. Pedestrians still traveled barefoot. Most naughty children used basins as boats to swim in it. Fishermen or held nets to catch fish, and could get dozens of catties every day. Families, old and young, could use this to survive. The Construction Bureau dredged the Menghe River this year, but the north section of the Menghe River was uniquely left out. I don't know why. With such heavy rains for days, there was no way out for the water, so the surrounding fields were all turned into swamps, and business was greatly affected. Now the township chief is preparing to report the famine. Since this rain disaster, food prices have risen sharply, and grains, melons, and vegetables have all doubled in price. It is truly a disaster that has not occurred in nearly ten years.

A Kidnapping Case Occurs in Gangzi Township

In the fifth li of Gangzi Township in the fourth district of Wuyi, the other night, unscrupulous people set up a stage to perform Tanhuang near the house of Gu Hong, the township chief. A farmer named Tan Gaoda has three sons. The eldest and second sons went out to watch Tanhuang. Tan and his 13-year-old youngest son slept at home. Because the two sons had not returned, the back door was not closed. In the middle of the night, two bandits suddenly came in through the back door, holding flashlights to shine. One bandit opened the curtain and pointed a gun at Gaoda, threatening him not to make a sound. The other bandit picked up his 13-year-old youngest son and still went to the back door. Afterwards, they searched everywhere, but there was still no news.

Zhenjiang

Zhu Jieshi's Case of Shooting an Innocent Person is Scheduled for Trial

Zhu Jieshi, the former police captain of Huaiyin County, mistakenly killed two farmers, Sun Deyuan and Jiang Diancheng, while suppressing bandits in Hongfuzhuang during his tenure. Knowing his mistake, not only did he not change, but he abandoned the bodies of Sun and Jiang in the river in an attempt to cover up his tracks. The masses heard about it and resisted, and also burned down the house of Li Shiqing, shot and injured the family members of the person in charge, and extorted huge sums of money. Afterwards, he fabricated charges and arrested him, arousing a major disturbance. Various groups in the county believed that Zhu was so rampant and extremely illegal, and organized the Hongfuzhuang Massacre Support Association to file a complaint in the province, and recommended representatives to appeal to various agencies to send a committee to investigate and verify, and escort Zhu and Detective Liu Yunpeng and attendant Li Yunpeng to the province, and transfer them to the court for investigation. The prosecution department had already summoned witnesses to open a court for investigation and prosecution in the criminal court. Subsequently, the prosecutor filed an appeal, which was delayed until now, and the interrogation could not be made public. It is now heard that Zhu Jieshi specially requested the court to expedite the conclusion of the case because he had been in custody for a long time. The Criminal Court, according to the complaint, in addition to notifying the defendant, also summoned the victims Li Shiqing, Fan Shilin, Hua Yongqin, and witnesses Qian Youzheng and other 11 people to open a court for trial publicly at 10:00 am on the 14th of this month. It is heard that Li Shiqing, who was summoned, had already arrived in the province yesterday to prepare to attend the court for interrogation when the time came.

Nantong

The Water Disaster Dispute in Dongxiang Has Not Ended

A major flood in Dongxiang, Nantong caused farmers upstream and downstream of Yuxi and Sanyu to engage in a decisive battle over opening the dam, resulting in multiple deaths and injuries. A lawsuit has been filed with the court. On the 11th, the county government, believing that the dispute there was unclear, specially commissioned Tao Junshan and Chen Zhongzhi to investigate the situation together with the Director of the Construction Bureau and the district chiefs to discuss a solution, so as to avoid causing further incidents.

Checking Old Strings to Investigate Embezzlement Cases

The Nantong Finance Bureau, which has been collecting field taxes since 1928, has been reported to have committed fraud. The Finance Department has ordered the county government to quickly order the original personnel of the Finance Bureau to go to the department on a specific date to check the old strings that were handed over, so as to thoroughly investigate the embezzlement case. The required travel expenses will be allocated from the collection fees by the Finance Bureau.

Implementing the Consolidation of Huainan Salt Land

The Ministry of Finance believes that the situation in Huainan is complex after the reclamation and has specially commissioned Hu Xingchi, Deputy Transportation Commissioner of Huainan, and Zhou Zonghua, Manager of the Yangzhou Audit Branch Office, to consolidate the Huainan salt land. At present, we must first clear the salt yard and kitchen land. We must determine where to cultivate, where to store grass, and leave it for frying, and we must register the cultivated and uncultivated salt ponds, as well as those that have been paid for and not paid for.

Rugao

Forced Opening of the Dam Shoots Farmers

Regarding water conservancy, the Huafeng Dam in Huafeng Town, Juegang, is in conflict with the interests of the local farmers. Now, due to a sudden major flood, the company sent the local defense regiment to forcefully open the dam with weapons. The local farmers, believing that it was in their best interests, gathered to oppose it, and a conflict broke out. The defense regiment shot and killed two farmers on the spot. The county government heard the news and has sent personnel to investigate.

The Zhoujiawei Gate Was Washed Away by Water

The Zhoujiawei Gate in Shizhuang County was washed away by the upstream water due to continuous heavy rain in recent days. Yesterday, many farmers were fishing there. Wu's son was watching there, and accidentally fell into the water and died.

Hangzhou

Revenue Collector Embezzles Huge Sums and is Imprisoned and Pursued

Shi Shaomei, the revenue collector of the 19th District of the Hangzhou Municipal Finance Bureau, was young and frivolous and made the wrong friends. He collected 1,720 yuan in taxes in March and April and went to Shanghai with two or three friends, spending the money extravagantly. The Finance Bureau pursued the original guarantors and merchants to recover the money. Shi had already returned to Hangzhou, so he was arrested and sent to the Public Security Bureau for transfer to the court. After investigation by Prosecutor Jiang, he confessed to the previous situation. The crime of embezzlement has been established, and he has been imprisoned for investigation and ordered to return the original money.

A Car Accident Occurs on the Hangping Highway

At around 5:00 pm yesterday, a No. 106 car was traveling from Haining to Hangzhou on the Yuangjiaba section of the Hangping Highway. The machinery suddenly broke down, and the car body crashed into the pond below, causing it to overturn. There were more than ten passengers in total, and five of them were injured. The Provincial Highway Administration was telegraphed to send a spare car to pick them up. The injured were taken to Dabo Guangji Hospital for treatment that night.

Ningbo

Loss from Careless Handling of Mail Packages is Still Small

The Xinjiangtian Wheel arrived in Yong from Shanghai at 5:00 pm the other day. It was unexpected that when the ship was passing through the Daji Ocean, blue smoke suddenly came out of the mail package. The shipowner was immediately notified and ordered all the sailors to put out the fire. Many mail packages were burned, and the rest were stained with water. Fortunately, the mail package was surrounded by thick iron sheets on all sides, so the ship body was not damaged. At 6:00 am yesterday, the ship safely arrived at Yong Port. As usual, the shipowner reported to the Zhejiang Maritime Customs Administration to send personnel to inspect it. It was deemed that there was no obstacle to the ship's sailing, so it was ordered to sail as usual. Most of the letters that were burned were ordinary letters, and the loss was still small.

Three Communists Escorted to the Province for Interrogation

Feng Zide and others, the Communists of Xiangshan County, have been wanted by the provincial government and have fled elsewhere. Now, they have secretly returned to their hometowns during the summer vacation. On the 8th of this month, the county government learned the truth and ordered the police to secretly arrest them. Feng Zide, Mu Guxi, and Lai Dazhi were arrested and escorted to Yong that day, and then transferred to the provincial capital for interrogation.

Letter

Letter from Jiangsu Provincial Hospital

Sir, I am writing to you regarding the Zhenjiang correspondence in your newspaper on July 10, which contained a report on the hospital president being released on bail. This is not only untrue, but also contains errors. The condition that Yi suffers from is syphilitic arthritis, which has lasted for nearly ten years. His feet are ulcerated and his limbs are twisted. All medicines have failed and he has long been disabled. Since entering our hospital, the ulcers have healed for a long time. He can now lie down, who was previously unable to do so. He can now stand, who was previously unable to do so. Only the virus is deep-rooted and the hip joint is permanently damaged, so he cannot move, as before. This is not as reported in your newspaper, (that his leg bones were reversed during surgery for external disease, causing him to be unable to move). As for the so-called use of gas to check, this is actually a misinterpretation of the Wassermann reaction test. Moreover, the Wassermann reaction is a method to check whether there is syphilis in the blood, and it is not like an X-ray machine that can see the bones. Based on this point, it can also be seen that it is deliberately fabricated. Other things, such as (but only testing and testing), are fabrications. In short, the case is extremely complex, and we have now filed a counterclaim according to law. In addition to waiting for a legal solution and expert appraisal, we have always admired your newspaper for upholding righteousness. We hereby write to you to request that you investigate and make corrections, so that we can clearly distinguish right from wrong. Jiangsu Provincial Hospital, July 7, 11.
