Local News

All Circles Will Hold a Meeting Today to Jointly Discuss Measures Against Japan

Meeting at the Municipal Chamber of Commerce at 2 PM

After the outbreak of anti-Chinese riots by Koreans, the industrial and commercial groups of this city have decided to convene various mass organizations at the Municipal Chamber of Commerce at 2 PM today to earnestly discuss measures against Japan together. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs telegraphed the representatives of the Korean Chinese Chamber of Commerce in Shanghai yesterday, stating that they had lodged a serious protest, but received a confidential letter from the Korean Chinese Chamber of Commerce, which described the horrific details of the Korean riots. The details are recorded as follows:

Telegram from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs

The Ministry of Foreign Affairs telegraphed a reply to Liu Zhongkui, representative of the Korean Chinese Chamber of Commerce in Incheon and Seoul, stating: Your submission has been noted. We have notified the Japanese Chargé d'Affaires and lodged a serious protest, and reserved negotiations. We have repeatedly telegraphed the Minister to Japan and the Consul General to Korea, requesting the Japanese authorities to protect and stop the riots. According to the telegram reply, the Japanese side expressed great apology and has ordered the police to do their best to suppress them, which can be calmed down. The Korean governor has not yet taken office, and there is someone in charge who will not shirk responsibility. In addition to continuing negotiations, I hope to convey this to all relevant parties. Ministry of Foreign Affairs.

Appeal from Shandong People by Telegram

(1) The Shandong Association in Shanghai telegraphed the Ministry of Foreign Affairs again yesterday, stating: Your Excellency Minister Wang of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, the steam telegram is for the Korean riots and the massacre of overseas Chinese. Please send personnel to negotiate and find a way to stop it, etc. It is hoped that this will be understood. Later, at 7 PM on the same day, a telegram was received from the Korean Wonsan Chamber of Commerce saying, "3,000 merchants and workers have taken refuge in the consulate, and the city is unstable," etc. According to this, after investigating, the Koreans are massacring overseas Chinese and are aggressively pressing forward. Our overseas Chinese are hanging by a thread and are in dire straits. If we do not quickly find a way to stop them, it is inevitable that the previous tragedy will be repeated. For this reason, we are sending another telegram to present our request. We beg you to seriously negotiate and find a way to stop them, so as to protect our compatriots and emphasize national rights. We cannot help but eagerly await your order. (1) The preparatory office of the Shandong Business Federation in Shanghai telegraphed: Your Excellency the National Government of Nanjing and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, the association has telegraphed the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce on the 8th regarding the case of Koreans killing overseas Chinese, requesting that the foreign affairs authorities negotiate strictly as soon as possible. (This is omitted) On the same day, there were also massacres of overseas Chinese in Busan and Wonsan. Those who took refuge in the Consulate General's Office were lucky to escape the net, but were subjected to exhaustion. The overseas Chinese in the eight provinces of Korea are on the verge of life and death every day. Calling to heaven is unanswered, and calling to earth is ineffective. Who is doing this for them? Who caused this? Clear-sighted people can see through the conspiracy. Thinking back to when Korea separated from our protection, it has been less than forty years. Why is there such irreconcilable hatred that they must destroy them to be willing? Who would dare to believe that there is no one giving instructions? The Wanpaoshan Incident occurred on June 1, and the Pyeongyang Massacre occurred on July 6. The brewing organization lasted for more than a month. With Japan's world-renowned police force supervising the Koreans who have been unwilling to die for decades, who would dare to believe that the police were unaware of the organization and brewing for more than a month? It can be blamed on the lack of prior awareness and the sudden outbreak of the incident, and the police were weak. Why is it that the same things are discovered in the massacres in Pyeongyang and Seoul, the same lack of prior awareness, and the same inability to suppress them afterwards? Furthermore, Seoul is a fundamental and important place, and the military strength should be different from other ports. Such a heavily guarded place, but blaming the military and police for being unable to suppress them, who would dare to believe? In short, Japan is using an indirect immigration policy to prevent our overseas Chinese from gaining a foothold in its colonies, so it is using this conspiracy to kill people with a borrowed knife to eliminate our overseas Chinese. At a time when the world respects humanity, there is such behavior. Where is our country's sovereignty? Where is international law? Where is international public opinion and sanctions? The association is a merchant organization, and in view of the fact that most of those who were massacred this time were merchants, and all of them were merchants from our Shandong Province, we are deeply concerned, and our words are naturally heartfelt. For this reason, we appeal to your government (department) to immediately telegraph Japan to quickly stop it, and to telegraph the International Court of Justice and the various leagues of the International League to promote humanity and denounce the riots. We are at a loss and cannot help but cry and beg.

The Overseas Chinese's Plight

Cao Jingyu, Executive Director of the Korean Association in Shanghai, told a reporter from the New Voice News Agency that since the outbreak of the anti-Chinese incident in Korea, a telegram has been received from overseas Chinese who fled to Yantai, stating that the Japanese authorities in Korea are withholding emergency telegrams from overseas Chinese merchants and strictly checking letters. All those mentioning Korean affairs will be withheld. Trains and ships are prohibited from Chinese riding back to their countries. Overseas Chinese have no way out. It is heard that Korean rice and grain shops are even preventing Chinese from buying them. Therefore, the association has decided to send representatives to the Shanghai Office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs again tomorrow to petition Foreign Minister Wang Zhengting, requesting that he quickly find a way to rescue the overseas Chinese.

Brutal Situation

The New Voice News Agency stated that it received a confidential letter from the Korean Chinese Chamber of Commerce yesterday, which roughly stated that after the Korean riots, the president of the Chinese Chamber of Commerce went to the Incheon Prefecture Office, requesting that troops be sent quickly to protect them. The Prefecture Office said that the Japanese police were handling the situation effectively and could definitely prevent any trouble. On the afternoon of that day, many overseas Chinese took refuge in the Chamber of Commerce and school buildings. The refugees were full of people, and the tragic situation was unbearable to see. At 8 PM, the Chinese shopkeepers on the Korean streets said that there were many Koreans gathering in groups, and the situation was very urgent, requesting protection. When the police arrived, the doors and windows of each house had been damaged. When they arrived, the Koreans attacked the Chinese streets again. The shops in various places were broken beyond recognition. Valuable goods were robbed, and cheap goods were thrown into the streets. Dozens of people were injured and many died. Two of them had their hearts taken out and their eyes gouged out. They arbitrarily set fires with kerosene. The Koreans used large axes, long poles, stones, knives, and wooden sticks as weapons. The Japanese officials protected them on the surface, but secretly sided with the Koreans.

The Riot Gradually Subsides

A certain merchant firm in this city recently received a telegram from Chinese merchants in Incheon stating that the anti-Chinese riots in Korea are gradually subsiding in places such as Seoul, Incheon, Jinnampo, and Sinuiju. It is reported that a representative of the Korean Governor-General's Office has apologized to our country's Consul-General in Korea. At the same time, Consul-General Zhang Weicheng requested the Governor-General's representative to restore the original state within a limited time, which has been agreed upon. On the 10th, investigators from Pyongyang returned to Beijing, reporting the tragic situation, causing universal grief. On the 11th, the Governor-General's representative continued to visit our Consul-General, answering all questions. Mr. Zhang strongly argued for the safety of the entire area, which the representative agreed to. However, refugees are lingering in various places, lacking funds and food, and many are falling ill, urgently needing relief. Consul-General Zhang has been inspecting the areas where Chinese reside for days. The number of casualties and losses suffered by the Chinese is currently under detailed investigation.

Yesterday's Yu Qiaqing Commemorative Meeting

The Grand Occasion on the Second Day

Yesterday was the second day of Mr. Yu Qiaqing's 50th Anniversary Celebration in Shanghai. The number of guests attending was even more enthusiastic than on the first day. Details are as follows:

Motorcade Parade

The motorcade parade for Mr. Yu Qiaqing's 50th Anniversary Celebration in Shanghai was held yesterday at 1 p.m. Before noon, the area in front of the Ningbo Fellow-Provincials Association was already packed with onlookers. The Shanghai Municipal Police specially dispatched Chinese and foreign detectives to maintain order. Automobiles from various organizations and people from all walks of life arrived one after another. Organizations participating included the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, the National Products Mall, the Ning Shao Company, the Chinese Seamen's Union, the Zhabei Charity Group, the Jiangwan Fire Brigade, the Securities and Commodities Exchange Brokers Association, the Songjiang Ning Shao Fellow-Provincials Association, the Da Xin Silk Store, and others. Prominent figures in Shanghai, such as Wang Xiaolai, Le Zhenbao, Wang Binyan, Kui Yanfang, Sun Meitang, Dong Xingsheng, Wu Zhihao, Xie Baosheng, He Shaoting, Fang Jiaobo, Lu Fengzhu, Chen Yiting, Chen Songyuan, Zhu Jingan, Tan Haiqiu, Hu Yongqi, and others, also participated. In total, there were over two hundred automobiles. At 1 p.m., Mao Heyuan, director of the motorcade parade, gave a speech of thanks to the various organizations and guests, stating that colleagues had initiated the motorcade parade to celebrate Mr. Yu Qiaqing's 50th anniversary of doing business in Shanghai because Mr. Yu Qiaqing had made great contributions and efforts to society, whether for the country or for the people, and was very worthy of celebration. He was very honored that representatives of various organizations and people from all walks of life had enthusiastically participated in the parade. On behalf of Mr. Yu, he thanked everyone. While Mr. Mao was speaking, Tianyi Film Company was filming. Immediately afterward, parade leaders Mao Heyuan and Shen Xiechen led the departure, with the conference's float at the forefront. The float prominently displayed the words "Motorcade Parade Celebrating Mr. Yu Qiaqing's 50th Anniversary in Shanghai," which was quite eye-catching. Police also dispatched foreign police cars to patrol and protect the procession. The parade proceeded according to the original route, winding like a long snake. The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, the National Products Mall, and the Da Xin Silk Store also had floats participating, which were also quite beautiful. Tianyi Film Company filmed along the way, and the crowds of onlookers caused traffic to be blocked. The parade returned to the racecourse for a photo shoot and dispersed. There were also quite a few automobiles that arrived late and were unable to participate.

Meeting Circumstances

Yesterday afternoon, after the motorcade parade, the meeting continued. Chairman Wang Xiaolai first had Yu Qiaqing report on the gifts received from various parties and the intention to prepare for the establishment of the Sanbei Hospital. He then expressed his gratitude to all the guests. Speakers who followed included Sun Hengfu, manager of the Siming Bank, Fang Jiaobo of the Ning Shao branch, Wen Lanting of the exchange, Liu Yaoting of the Sanbei Company, and Wu Zhihao. Finally, Chairman Wang Xiaolai gave a closing speech, and the meeting ended.

Summary of Speeches

(1) Mayor Zhang's speech briefly stated that Mr. Qiaqing's life's work had been detailed in the special publication, and Mr. Qiaqing himself had described his fifty years of experience in detail to us, so there was no need for him to elaborate. He dared to say that there was not a single person in Shanghai, whether Chinese or foreign, who did not know Mr. Qiaqing. There must be a reason why he was held in such high esteem, which was that he had overcome fifty years of hardship and effort to create today's history and environment, and to produce today's grand celebration. Today's commemorative meeting was not just because we usually respectfully call him "Old Qiaqing" or "Old Shanghai." There were others present who had been in Shanghai for more than fifty years, so why were we not holding a commemoration for them, but only for Mr. Qiaqing? Of course, it was not just because he had a wide circle of friends, and we were just gathering to join in the fun. It was because Mr. Qiaqing had made great contributions and blessings to the country and society in the past fifty years, so today's commemoration held great meaning in the speaker's personal opinion. First, it expressed admiration for Mr. Qiaqing's fifty years of effort. He had known Mr. Qiaqing for twenty years, starting during the 1911 Revolution, when they shared hardships. Mr. Qiaqing also enthusiastically participated in the Second Revolution. After the Revolutionary Army began the Northern Expedition in 1926 and reached the Southeast, the government received much support from Mr. Qiaqing. Although he had only known Mr. Qiaqing for twenty years, he knew a lot about his life. Now, from the perspective of twenty years of friendship, judging Mr. Qiaqing's fifty years of effort, Mr. Qiaqing's life's work was enough to be a model for future generations. The meaning of the commemoration was not to praise an individual, but to take the opportunity to publicize his achievements as a guideline and path for future generations to strive for. Therefore, today's meeting was of great significance. Speaking of the rise and fall of a country, in addition to the rule of law, there was also the issue of people. Looking at all countries, in all fields and in all kinds of careers, there were elders participating in them. The so-called elders did not refer to their old age, but to the fact that they had devoted their entire lives to a certain career and ultimately achieved success, were respected by all fields, and were loved by the people. Thomas Edison, the American inventor of electricity, was such a figure. He only knew about his career and not about himself. In our country, it was not easy to find an elder who had devoted his entire life to good deeds. Mr. Qiaqing was a rare exception. We still hoped that Mr. Qiaqing would continue to work hard, as he reported, and take responsibility for abolishing unequal treaties for the country and canceling the nation's deed of sale. Mr. Qiaqing had worked hard on his career for decades as if it were one day, and he still did not give up his hard work to carry out his long-cherished ambition. It was hoped that colleagues would gather under Mr. Qiaqing's leadership and fight forward. The speaker presented Mr. Qiaqing with the words "Rising Like the Sun" as a memento, with that meaning. In China, whenever there was a happy event, people always said, "May you grow old together for a hundred years." It was hoped that in another fifty years, we could hold another "Centennial Commemorative Meeting" for Mr. Qiaqing. The speaker respectfully offered his sincere blessings. (2) Wang Xiaolai's speech briefly stated that today's 50th anniversary celebration for Mr. Qiaqing's life in Shanghai was a rare event. Only Mr. Zhu Baosan had ever had one like it, but it was not as grand as today's. Words of praise and admiration were already dazzling and beautiful. Mr. Qiaqing was sixty-five years old this year. Everyone in Shanghai, whether they were from Shanghai or had come to Shanghai, knew Mr. Qiaqing. He came to Shanghai at the age of fifteen, when he should have been called Young Qiaqing. Fifteen to fifty to fifty to fifteen was to show the cycle of infinity. Thinking of Old Qiaqing, thinking of Young Qiaqing, from Young Qiaqing to Old Qiaqing, he just happened to become an old youth. The so-called old youth was not just a fabrication, but should be based on evidence. It was not as good as wishing someone a long life, always wishing them a life as long as Nanshan Mountain, never aging, or wishing someone happiness, always wishing them a hundred years of harmony and five generations of prosperity, which may not necessarily be realized. However, the so-called old youth of Mr. Qiaqing had concrete evidence. The proverb referred to an old youth as someone who was old but acted like a youth, which was the same as being old and strong. Like an old youth, opening flowers in the late autumn and winter scenery made them even more brilliant and beautiful. Furthermore, according to the old youth, it was also called the "Ten Sample Brocade." Mr. Qiaqing encompassed all aspects of the country, society, commerce, and public welfare. He was eloquent and heartfelt in matters of politics, diplomacy, local charity, and so on. According to ancient sayings, the "Ten Sample Brocade" was something Xiaolai and Qiaqing recognized at the end of the Guangxu era. They had been together for more than twenty years, and he had never seen Qiaqing wear a leather coat in winter or carry a fan in summer. He had not changed until now. His spirit of not fearing the heat and cold was truly admirable. He never paid attention to his clothing or food and was always busy, but he became healthier the busier he was. He associated with young people in the evening, without distinguishing between old and young, all year round, often returning late at night, day after day for decades. This was like the "Ten Sample Brocade" of the old youth, which could withstand frost and cold and become an extraordinary product, so he could do extraordinary things and open an extraordinary celebration. Mr. Qiaqing could truly be regarded as the flower of the Republic of China and the auspicious sign of the country.

Proposed Matters

1. Chen Liangyu proposed that public groups should be responsible for preparing and erecting a bronze statue for Mr. Yu Qiaqing to express respect and admiration. 2. Mr. Yu Zongzhou proposed that the Shanghai Municipal Council should open a Yu Qiaqing Road in the concession to leave a memorial. 3. Shao Ruxin proposed that a commemorative meeting should be held for Mr. Yu Qiaqing every ten years in the future, and a centennial celebration should be held in another fifty years. All the guests applauded and agreed.

Tomorrow's French Democratic Memorial

On the 14th of this month, the French Democratic Memorial Day, French officials and merchants in Shanghai originally planned to hold a lantern parade on the evening of the 13th and a celebration ceremony on the 14th. Public Safety Bureau Plans to Conduct Physical Examinations of Foreigners Entering China

Shanghai is the center of national land and water transportation. Foreigners who come to China by boat must first disembark in Shanghai. Therefore, Shanghai is a very important location. However, the government authorities have always allowed foreigners to enter and exit freely. Not only were foreigners' bodies not examined, but travel passports were only required starting May 1 this year. Since the passport inspection office began its work, it has caught many people from various European and American countries entering China without passports, and they have all been sent back to their countries one after another. Recently, the Shanghai Municipal Public Safety Bureau has also seen that there are many types of infectious diseases from abroad, such as venereal diseases and eye diseases, all of which are transmitted from abroad. In order to pay attention to the health of the Chinese people, we must pay special attention to the health of foreigners entering China. Therefore, it has been decided to conduct physical examinations of foreigners entering China, and preparations will begin soon. It is reported that the method in the future will be to have the passport inspectors and medical personnel inspect the foreign vessels at the port of entry.

The Process of Sugar Merchants' Petition in Beijing

Request to Amend the Draft Agreement for the Sino-Cuban Joint Sugar Factory

Because the draft agreement for the Sino-Cuban joint venture China National Sugar Manufacturing Factory, which was organized by the Ministry of Industry, contained many clauses that would cede national sovereignty, the sugar merchants in Shanghai petitioned in Beijing to request corrections to protect national rights and save losses. They have now returned to Shanghai. The petition process, the content of the draft agreement, and the status of the sugar industry in the world and China are described separately below.

Petition Process

The Sugar Trade Association appointed representatives Zheng Zenan, Yang Wenshao, Jiang Yachen, and others to present a petition in Beijing on the 7th, requesting the government to quickly amend or cancel the draft agreement for the Sino-Cuban joint sugar factory to avoid the loss of national sovereignty. Wang Pinsheng, Secretary of the Executive Yuan, received them and said that the Minister of Finance was currently in Shanghai and the Executive Yuan would pay attention to the matter. After a detailed discussion at the Executive Council meeting on the 14th, it would be reviewed and approved. Please wait for the instructions. Legislative Yuan President Shao Yuanchong was out on official business, and a staff member received them, saying that the various reasons stated in the petition would be used as reference when the industrial review group met to discuss the matter. Zhao Jinqing, Vice Minister of Industry, received them and said that if the draft agreement for the Sino-Cuban joint sugar factory did indeed cede national sovereignty and affect the livelihood of the sugar industry, the Ministry would take it into consideration. However, there may be misunderstandings in what was stated in the petition, such as the sales rights not being given to the Cubans. The China National Sugar Manufacturing Company was currently suspended, and sugar merchants could continue to operate to develop Chinese enterprises. If there were difficulties in raising capital, the government would do its best to assist. The sugar merchant representatives stated that they did not oppose the principle of cooperation, but national sovereignty could not be lost. If the draft agreement was amended and Cuba did not agree to lend money, the sugar factory would be wholly state-owned, and all capital would be filled by the Ministry of Finance with appropriate public bonds. The principal repayment fund for these public bonds would be added to the national sugar import tax. Vice Minister Zhao expressed acceptance of the sugar merchants' opinions. As for the China International Sugar Company organized by Cuba, it would establish distribution offices everywhere to sell the output of the joint sugar factory, but there was no fact that the company was responsible for the sales. The representatives were satisfied and returned to Shanghai by night train on the 8th.

Content of the Draft Agreement

The content of the signed draft agreement for the Sino-Cuban joint sugar factory is roughly divided into six chapters and contains a total of thirty-four articles. It is named the China National Sugar Manufacturing Factory, with the purpose of developing the domestic sugar industry in China. The sugar factory is resolved to be state-owned and managed in accordance with the laws of the Republic of China. The capital is five million gold yuan. There will be one factory director and one deputy factory director, divided into three departments: business, accounting, and engineering. The factory director, deputy factory director, and head of the business accounting department will be Chinese. The head of the engineering department and the deputy head of accounting may be appointed by Cuba from other countries. The factory must jointly certify and pay the monthly payments and budgets with Cuban accountants and issue type A bonds (for factory machinery) totaling no more than US$5 million and type B bonds (to repay sugar payments) totaling no more than US$15 million. Cuba will be given a 0.5% handling fee by China for the purchase of raw materials. The pure profit of the sugar factory will be calculated as a percentage, giving Cuba 5% as a consolation fee. The raw sugar required by the sugar factory will be purchased by Cuba.

World Sugar Industry

Deng Zenan, standing member of the Shanghai Sugar Trade Association, told a New Voices reporter yesterday that Cuba is the country with the most sugar production in the western hemisphere, shipping 4.6 million tons in 1919. The sugar produced in Cuba is all raw sugar, mostly supplied to the United States because the United States uses raw sugar. In the eastern hemisphere, it is Java in the Dutch East Indies, shipping 3.1 million tons in 1919. In recent years, due to oversupply, prices have fallen sharply. Cuba advocates contacting world sugar producing countries to restrict production. Last year, it sent representatives to Java, Japan, Italy, and other countries to investigate production and sales. On April 1 this year, a joint meeting of world sugar producing countries was held in Belgium to discuss restrictions. Last year, Cuba had 600,000 tons of raw sugar in storage. It was resolved that only Australia and China were allowed to transport and sell it.

Chinese Sugar Industry

China imported a total of 13 million piculs of sugar in 1919, with Shanghai accounting for 7 million piculs. Refined sugar accounted for one-half, and green sugar, raw sugar, and coarse sugar together accounted for one-half. Cuba's raw sugar imports were 14,000 tons, totaling 240,000 piculs. At the end of last year, there were still 66,000 piculs in storage. Our country has never produced sugar. This time, the Association asked the government to amend or cancel the draft agreement for the Sino-Japanese joint sugar factory, which was entirely a patriotic movement because the draft agreement contained provisions that ceded national sovereignty. However, it had nothing to do with the livelihood of the industry and did not contain any other effects. Therefore, we hope that the government will accommodate the sugar merchants' requests and correct them.

Japan and the US Compete in Pacific Shipping

Japanese Ships Lower Prices to Counter American Vessels

American Giant Vessels Coming

The American company Dollar Steamship Lines is building two of the largest postal ships, each 32,000 tons, at a cost of US$60 million, to operate on the Pacific route from Shanghai, hoping to remedy the current economic downturn. The company has now received a cable from its head office stating that the hull and passenger accommodations of the first ship, the President Hoover, have been completed and it is expected to arrive in Shanghai in September. The ship is extremely fast, exceeding the speed of existing Sino-American vessels, capable of traveling at over 21 nautical miles per hour. The ship is also equipped with airplanes for delivering express mail. The second ship, the President Coolidge, is scheduled to arrive in Shanghai and begin operations in early December.

Japan Mail Price Drop

Since merging with Toyo Kisen Kaisha and building seven new Pacific vessels, the Nippon Yusen Kaisha (NYK Line) has intended to dominate the Sino-American route. With the Osaka Shosen Kaisha (OSK Line) vessels on the San Francisco and Seattle routes now also merged into NYK Line, the company's ambition to monopolize Pacific shipping rights has grown stronger. Upon hearing that the two new Dollar Steamship Lines vessels are about to begin operations, and recognizing that their size and speed surpass those of NYK Line's vessels, making them formidable competitors, NYK Line has been discussing countermeasures for days. It has decided to drastically reduce fares by approximately 15% before the arrival of the two American vessels to counter them. The new prices will take effect on August 1st. The new and old prices for various ships are listed below (in US dollars):

Taiyo Maru New Taiyo Maru, etc.

Destination New Price Old Price New Price Old Price

San Francisco 173 203 155 173

Honolulu 135 160 120 135

Tax-Exempt Native Cloth Seized During Transport

Trade Association Petitions Ministries of Finance and Industry for Release

Regarding the seizure of tax-exempt native cloth being transported by members of the local Native Cloth Trade Association by the Tax Collection Office stationed at the Customs, the association yesterday submitted another petition to both the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry, stating: "Regarding the seizure of tax-exempt native cloth being transported, which has been detained by the Tax Collection Office stationed at the Customs for over a month, causing anxiety among merchants and requesting prompt release to avoid danger. Previously, the association received a telegram regarding the tax-exempt hand-woven native cloth being transported to the eastern provinces. According to reports from merchants, the goods were detained by the Tax Collection Office stationed at the Customs, which has been a month, affecting finances and creating a dangerous situation in the market. The general tax exemption for native cloth has been resolved by the National Government and has been notified by your ministry. Since the establishment of the consolidated tax, cotton yarn already subject to the consolidated tax will not be subject to double taxation. On May 19th, the Ministry of Finance approved a general tax exemption for customs duties, with a notice on file. This native cloth is a secondary industry for farmers in Jiangsu Province and is mostly used by people in the eastern provinces. Recently, imported cloth has been encroaching on the eastern provinces, becoming dominant. The National Government, recognizing this, has exempted taxes to reduce costs for merchants and restore livelihoods. The association has repeatedly submitted petitions for customs duty exemptions, detailing the production and sales areas, requesting simultaneous exemptions, not for the purpose of Shanghai exports, with the intention of shifting the burden to others. According to a report from merchant Zhu Limen, the eastern provinces previously had no native cloth taxes and misunderstood the consolidated tax, believing it was unexpected. According to regulations, the consolidated tax is paid in the production area, and then the goods can be transported anywhere without double taxation, regardless of the production or sales area. The regulations are clear and can be reviewed. In short, this native cloth is a completely domestic product, and both the supply and demand sides are mostly poor households. The country and the people are closely linked, and Jiangsu Province and the eastern provinces are also closely linked. We beseech your ministry to consider promoting trade and provide assistance by urgently sending a telegram to the Finance Department of Liaoning Province, explaining the reasons for the tax exemption for all native cloth, as well as the promulgation of consolidated tax regulations and the one-tax-per-item system, to ensure simultaneous tax exemption throughout the country, to maintain national credibility and improve people's livelihoods, for which we would be immensely grateful."

Sales Offices for Manufactured Goods Should Be Subject to Business Tax

The City Chamber of Commerce previously received a letter from the Science Instrument Museum, stating that all manufactured goods leaving their place of manufacture should still be subject to sales tax, which is inconsistent with the principle of one tax per item, and requested a reasoned argument. The Chamber then sent a telegram to the Ministry of Finance requesting instructions. Now, the Ministry of Finance's Fu Zi No. 6614 Yang Dai telegram states: "The Yang Dai telegram is acknowledged. Upon investigation, if a manufacturer directly wholesales manufactured goods from the factory, it constitutes a wholesale business directly established by the factory and should be subject to business tax according to the manufacturing industry. If manufactured goods have left their place of manufacture and are sold in sales offices, whether owned by the same manufacturer or the same firm, they should be subject to business tax according to the sales industry. The above information is hereby communicated for your information."

City Chamber of Commerce Investigates Customs of Pledged Factory Machinery

No Need to Transfer Possession of Machinery

The City Chamber of Commerce replied yesterday to the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court, stating: "With reference to your letter of June 20th, in which the court is handling a case that requires investigation into whether there are customs in this port regarding the granting of security interests in factory machinery without the need to transfer possession, the chamber has received your letter and dispatched personnel to investigate the banking and monetary industries and sent inquiries. The findings are now described in detail as follows: (1) In the loan contract, in addition to the guarantor, the borrower (i.e., the factory) specifies that the machinery is used as collateral for the loan. After the contract is established, the ownership is transferred to the lender. However, for the sake of maintaining its business, the borrower can establish a loan agreement to continue borrowing the original machinery from the lender (but there are also cases where a loan agreement is not established; see item 2). (2) After the borrower and lender enter into a loan agreement, there is no need to transfer ownership. The lender simply sends personnel to be stationed in the factory to supervise its operations. (3) If the pledged items are the factory base, factory buildings, and machinery, only the factory base needs to be transferred, and the buildings and machinery are listed separately in the pledge document, and the procedures are completed without the need to transfer possession of the machinery. All information regarding the customs of pledged machinery in this city is hereby provided. Please take note."

More Local News on the Following Page

Page 11

Local News Two

Continuous Rain

Fears of Another Famine

The continuous rain in Shanghai for over a week, with thunderstorms and heavy rain yesterday, may lead to another famine if the weather does not clear up soon. The following is a summary of what has been heard:

Western Shanghai

Northwest Shanghai, including Xin Jing, Zhu Zhai, and Zhen Ru, and the areas bordering Qingpu and Jiading, which are naturally low-lying, have seen farmland turn into swamps due to the heavy rains. Newly planted rice seedlings are submerged in water and will likely float up and turn yellow (what the locals call "floating yellow seedlings"). The planted cotton, watermelons, and various vegetables have also suffered severe damage. Although the villagers have dug ditches to drain the fields, they cannot discharge the water due to high river levels. The open spaces in Xiaoshadu, Zhoujiaqiao, and the northern part of the Bund are also deeply flooded. The grass sheds built by the people from Jiangbei have become small rivers, and meals are consumed in the water, which is a very pitiful sight.

Small Steamers Suspended

Local river steamship companies on North Suzhou Road, such as Zhaoshang, Laogongmao, and Tai Dong, which operate routes to Changshu, Kunshan, Dangkou, and other ports, as well as the small steamers from Kunshan to Changshu and Qingyang Port to Changshu, have temporarily suspended passenger services and cargo transportation since the previous day due to the sudden rise in water levels by several feet in the rivers, the loosening of the mud banks on both sides, which cannot withstand the waves, and the submersion of most of the small bridges, with the water level being too high under the bridges for passage.

Thunderstorm Electrocution News

Since 5 PM on the 6th of this month, Shanghai has been experiencing thunderstorms and heavy rain, lasting for a week. The weather has not cleared, with continuous cloud cover. Although the sun occasionally appears briefly, it soon disappears. There are frequent rumblings of thunder, and intermittent showers continue. The situation has been particularly bad since the evening before yesterday, with thunder continuing throughout the night and heavy rain. The rain continued yesterday evening, and the weather has not cleared. The room is unusually hot and humid, and many items are moldy. The following is a summary of electrocution incidents from yesterday morning: (1) In Ximu Bridge, Li Jiazhai, west of Luodian Town, a farmer, Li Atu, had a yellow cow suddenly electrocuted and killed in the cowshed at around 3 AM. (2) In a dilapidated temple in the countryside of Liuhe, a statue was inexplicably struck by lightning and destroyed.

More News on the Successful Rescue of Fu Aitang and Others from Kidnapping

Recounting the Incident of the Arrest

Captain Lu Commended and Rewarded

Yesterday's report stated that the fifth district, third precinct of Zhabei rescued the hostages Fu Aitang and Lu Hongfu from a kidnapping boat in the Tan Jiaqiao River on Ouyang Road, and arrested one male and one female kidnapper. It is now known that the cause of the successful rescue was that one week prior, Gao Wansheng and Qi Haitian, leaders of the Shanghai Public Security Bureau's Detective Team, received a confidential report from an informant stating that kidnappers Zhou Yuxi and others had kidnapped five hostages in Wujiang County, Suzhou, in April of the lunar calendar year, and were hiding them on a boat, secretly coming to Shanghai. It was discovered that the kidnapper's wives, Tao Musi and Zhu Bianshi, were frequenting the Nanmatou Xuejia Bang Road area. If these kidnapper's wives were arrested and interrogated, they would reveal the location of the hostages. Leader Gao immediately reported to Captain Lu, who ordered the leader to take the informant. In the afternoon of the same day, at 3 PM, the informant led them to the Nanmatou area. While walking along Xue Zi Bang Road, they spotted the kidnapper's wives Tao Musi and Zhu Bianshi sipping tea in a small teahouse. After the informant identified them, they were immediately arrested and taken to the team. Tao Musi provided evasive statements during the interrogation. When questioned, Zhu Bianshi revealed that the hostages were hidden in a small Jiangbei boat in the Tan Jiaqiao River behind Ouyang Road. Additional team leaders Su Sheng and Han Ruisheng, detectives Wang Shunbao and Han Jingxiang, secret agents Jiang Jinxiang and Xia Xiuying, and others were assigned to arrest the kidnapper's wife Zhu Bianshi at the address. At 6 PM, they cooperated with the police from the fifth district, third precinct, to make the arrests. However, as the detectives were walking on the bridge, they were spotted by the kidnappers on the boat, who immediately fled ashore. As a result, the hostages Fu Aitang and Lu Hongfu were rescued from under the cabin floor of the kidnapper's boat, and the kidnapper's wife Chen Zhushi was arrested. At the same time, the kidnapper Xu Yunzhen was also arrested. They were all interrogated. The two hostages provided detailed accounts of their kidnapping and everything that happened. The arrested kidnappers all confessed to the crimes without denial. After the case was solved, Director Chen specially approved a commendation and a major award for Captain Lu, and the other contributing officers will be rewarded separately after the case is concluded.

After investigation, the court found Ma Pan and Sun Xiaosan guilty and sentenced them to two months of forced labor each, to be served in prison. Recently, their terms expired, and Ma Runxi went to the prison to bring his wife back home for reconciliation. However, Ma Runxi recently filed a lawsuit with the District Court Prosecutor's Office, accusing Pan of improper conduct and requesting an investigation. Madam Ma Pan also submitted a petition to the District Court Mediation Office, requesting a divorce, stating that she had been subjected to unbearable abuse and insults. Ma Runxi hired lawyer Liu Shiqi to respond. Yesterday, Judge Chen Bingxin held a mediation hearing. The petitioner, Madam Ma Pan, stated that she was 23 years old, from Funing, and requested permission for a divorce, intending to support herself in the future. She added that she had suffered unjustly during her two-month prison sentence and found it difficult to live with her husband. The opposing party, Ma Runxi, did not appear, but his lawyer, Liu Shiqi, stated that the petitioner had committed adultery and that after her sentence, Ma Runxi had gone to the prison to bring her back, hoping she would reform. However, she continued her affair with Sun Xiaosan. Therefore, Ma Runxi had filed a lawsuit with the court, requesting a thorough investigation. Regarding the divorce, the opposing party was adamantly opposed. The judge, seeing that mediation had failed, instructed Madam Ma Pan to file a formal lawsuit separately.

Yang Lanying and Li Youcai

Regrettably, Both Under Twenty Years Old

Yang Changyin, from Funing and residing in Rihui Port, filed a complaint with the Second District Police Station, stating that his daughter, Lanying, 17 years old, had been jointly enticed and raped by the brothers Li Youke and Li Youcai, and was currently staying at the Gongxing Inn on Xujiahui Road. He requested their arrest. The police were dispatched and arrested Li Youke, Li Youcai, and Yang Lanying. Lanying confessed that she loved Li Youcai's gentle nature and had been in love with him since last year, vowing to be together. Because her stubborn father refused to agree to their marriage, she ran away and stayed at the inn. She denied any relationship with Li Youke. Li Youcai confessed that they were in a free love relationship and that to become a married couple, he and Lanying had hidden in the inn to proceed with the marriage. Li Youke denied the allegations of joint enticement and rape. Because the case involved the enticement of a woman under 20 years old, they were transferred to the District Court for investigation.

Returning Home to Visit Relatives with Nowhere to Settle

Living in Poverty, He Resort to This Measure

Yesterday afternoon at around 3:00 PM, a man suddenly appeared at Pier No. 10 near Guan Bridge in the Nanshi area and, taking advantage of the lack of attention, jumped into the Huangpu River. A patrol officer from the Pier Branch of the First District General Office of the Public Safety Bureau saw this and quickly called for nearby boatmen to rescue the man from the water. After being saved, he was taken back to the station. During the preliminary interrogation, the man claimed to be Zhu Guiren, 37 years old, from Hunan. He had previously served as an adjutant in the Fifth Route General Headquarters of the National Revolutionary Army. He resigned last year to return home to visit relatives. However, upon arriving in his hometown, he found that the area had been heavily disturbed by the Red Bandits and had nowhere to settle. He was forced to return to Shanghai, hoping to find a new job. However, he had been delayed until now without any success. Lacking any income, his life had become increasingly difficult, leading him to desperation. Feeling that there was no joy in this world, he had resorted to this measure. He requested understanding. He was ordered to prepare a document and send it to the City Public Safety Bureau for resettlement.

The China Harmonica Association Adds Summer Classes

The China Harmonica Association, located at 168 Sichuan Road, has been renovated internally since President Wang Qingxun decided to continue running it, with perfect equipment. To promote the popularity of harmonica music during the summer vacation, in response to requests from all walks of life, a "Special Summer Class" has been added, divided into two groups, A and B. Group A meets every Monday, Tuesday, Thursday, and Friday from 12:45 PM to 1:45 PM. Group B meets every Saturday and Sunday from 2:00 PM to 4:00 PM. Both groups use special teaching methods and can learn to play in one month. The fee is four yuan per person, including lecture notes and sheet music. Harmonica members provide their own harmonicas, each costing about three and a half yuan. The Association sells them. Anyone who loves this music, regardless of gender, can go to the Association to register and join. The deadline for starting classes is the 16th.

Asia Oil Company's Oil Tanker Sinks Ningbo Fishing Boat

Losses of Approximately 40,000 Yuan

The Ningbo fishing boat Jin Wanli was carrying over 2,320 dan of cargo, including tallow, bone, pit sand, and barrel sand, from Zhenjiang to Ningbo. Yesterday morning at around 4:00 AM, the boat was sailing near the black buoy of the Wusong Paotai Bay when an Asia Oil Company iron-hulled oil tanker, sailing outbound, mistakenly entered the wrong lane. The fishing boat captain, Wang Ashun, seeing this, quickly turned to avoid it, but it was too late. The fishing boat was struck in the middle and immediately split in two, sinking to the bottom of the sea. All thirteen crew members fell into the water. Fortunately, they were spotted by a patrol boat from the Jianghai Customs River Division, which immediately sped forward and rescued all the people from the water. Only one crew member, Chen, was injured. The entire cargo, worth approximately 30,000 yuan, and the boat itself, worth approximately 8,000 yuan, were lost. Zhou Xiexing Company has reported this to the Customs Marine Affairs Department, requesting serious negotiations with the Asia Oil Company. The River Division patrol boat believed that if the oil tanker had not made a small turn and entered the wrong lane, the accident would not have occurred. Therefore, the two pilots of the tanker were detained on the spot for questioning.

Abusing an Apprentice

Sentenced to a Fine of 150 Yuan

Ye Zaitang, a Yongbo native apprentice (16 years old) at the leather suitcase shop at 124 Peng Road, was severely beaten with a rattan cane by his master, Dong Xingshou, on the afternoon of the 6th of this month for being unruly at work, causing injuries all over his body. His hands were tied behind his back with hemp rope, preventing him from moving. He was later released by his fellow worker, Qian Agen, and his wife. After Ye Xianzheng, Ye Zaitang's uncle-grandfather, heard about the incident, he reported it to the Hongkou police station the other day. The police sent Chinese and foreign detectives to arrest the master, Dong Xingshou, along with the ropes and rattan cane. They were taken to the Third Criminal Court of the Special District Court. The police lawyer, Li Zhishan, presented the case, stating that the defendant should not have been so cruel. If the apprentice had made a mistake, his father or introducer could have been notified to take him back. Therefore, he requested the court to impose an appropriate punishment. Ye Xianzheng, the plaintiff, also submitted a complaint, and the apprentice, Ye Zaitang, showed the court his severe injuries. The red and purple marks on his back and legs were evident. Under questioning, the defendant admitted that he had beaten Ye because he had previously run away with leather goods. He was afraid that he would run away again, so he tied him up for about half an hour before being released. Qian Agen, a fellow worker, testified to the same effect. After verifying the confessions, Judge Xiao Xiefei sentenced Dong Xingshou to a fine of 150 yuan. If he chose imprisonment instead of paying the fine, it would be calculated at two yuan per day. The rattan cane and ropes were confiscated. The police lawyer, Li, requested that the defendant remain in custody during the appeal period. The court approved the request.

Unexpectedly,

he saw Wang Dushi at her house. Shen, realizing that these people were colluding to release a dove, was even more angry. Various Industries Request Relief from Obstacles to the Implementation of the New System of Weights and Measures

Customs Still Uses the Old System, Making Customs Declarations Inconvenient

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce received letters from the Flower Trade Association, the North-South Goods Exchange Association, and the Cured Meat Trade Association, requesting relief from the obstacles to the implementation of the new system of weights and measures, and forwarded them to the Social Affairs Bureau. The letter stated that the unified system of weights and measures in the city was scheduled to be implemented on July 1st. This matter concerns the overall commercial situation. Previously, during the general meeting of the Chamber of Commerce, it was publicly discussed that various industries should report their difficulties in writing for forwarding, showing great concern for the commercial situation and leadership. It is understood that revising the system of weights and measures is a new policy for the whole country, and the undersigned should comply with it. However, it is found that the goods sold, produced, transported, and distributed by the undersigned are closely related to customs declarations. At present, customs measurements still use the old system. All customs declarations, weighing, entering the warehouse, and loading are inconsistent. It is also not possible to convert them one by one, and accounting will inevitably become chaotic, leading to disputes. This is the first obstacle to prior change. Foreign trade and measurement have not changed. If the goods shipped and loaded are calculated according to the old system, it will not match the original weight of the store. If it is calculated according to the new system, it will not match the catties of other places. If you want to separately convert and indicate, it is not only troublesome, but also easy to make mistakes in the accounts and prices, confusing and unclear, and there is no way to take the standard, which will inevitably have a major impact. This is the second obstacle to prior change. The weights and prices of goods from other ports are based on the old system. Customs declarations and warehouses are mostly in the concession, which still follows the old practices. If the new system of customs forms and warehouse forms are used, the goods will not match, and there will be differences in the registration and filing. This is the third obstacle to prior change. In addition, the customs of the undersigned range from dozens of catties to two or three hundred catties. Each scale has at least two ropes, and the more there are three ropes. Because the goods are different, their uses are also different. The scales are also trained from a young age, so they can work quickly. Now the scales set in the testing institute only have one rope. I have requested to install new scales according to the old style, so that it can be applied, but it has not been done as desired. According to Yun, it is difficult to divide and order each scale with two ropes, not to mention three ropes. In fact, it is also impossible. Those who are called the order of heavy ones have nothing to use for light goods, and those who are called light ones cannot call heavy pieces. There are occasional extremely heavy pieces, which cannot be used without a sky scale as usual. How will those who use hooks to call be handled? This is the fourth obstacle to immediate change. All these four items have a common relationship, and the most difficult fact, other industries have different situations, and there are many kinds of difficulties that cannot be listed. In short, the measurement is related to national legislation, and it must be implemented. It should be diligently followed, but because it is related to the overall commercial situation, the circumstances are described in detail, and it is hoped that it will be forwarded and requested to be relaxed a little, so that it can be followed, etc. According to the 7th report, the Ministry of Finance has ordered the National Tariff Commission to review and reply to the new system of weights and measures used by the Customs. It is the implementation period. It is still far away, and the provinces and cities promote the new system, according to the original scheduled time, there are priorities, and Shanghai City has not been able to connect with it. It is the difficulties of the Guild and so on, which are indeed unavoidable facts. How should we consider appropriate remedial measures? Please ask Jun Bureau to give detailed instructions, so that they can be followed. The use of single ropes in the use of scales is very obstructive when exercising. According to the request of the Candle Industry Guild, the old system of weights and measures that has been forwarded for temporary destruction is also based on the proposal of the Dianye Guild, which is included in the resolution of the General Assembly. I have presented it to Jun Bureau for approval, and the Guild is asked to make a request in writing. I hereby ask Jun Bureau to forward it to the Testing Institute and investigators for proper handling.

Epidemics in the City are Gradually Increasing

Citizens are Advised to Take Note

The weather has been cloudy and rainy for several days, with alternating cold and heat. The number of epidemics in the city is increasing. Jiang Shijun, the daughter of Jiang Xiahun, residing at 1199 Siwenli, Xinzha Road, suddenly clenched her teeth, foamed at the mouth, and lost consciousness on the evening of the 11th of this month. Her mother thought it was fever and asked someone to scrape her back and the insides of her wrists, leaving red and purple marks and blood stains, but it was ineffective. By 8:00 AM yesterday morning, she was breathing rapidly and was on the verge of death. She was sent to the Chinese Red Cross Epidemic Hospital on the right side of the New World for treatment. Wang Zhenchuan, the doctor on duty, immediately performed surgery such as injections. Soon, her mouth and eyes opened, and she was able to drink medicine. In a few minutes, she was able to speak. Another woman with the same symptoms was also treated by hospital doctors Zhou Hongzhang and Zhang Danqing and fully recovered.

Workers at Pudong Hengda Yarn Factory Strike for Two Hours

Workers at the Pudong Hengda Yarn Factory were dissatisfied because the factory only replied to the union in a letter within 24 hours, refusing to reinstate six workers, including A Da. At 9:00 AM the other day, all the workers went on strike for two hours to show their solidarity and urge the capitalists to come to their senses. The factory sent representatives to ask the union to resume work temporarily and discuss the matter after the manager returned to the factory. The union advised the workers to resume work temporarily and after hearing that the manager had not returned to the factory at 9:00 PM, the workers became angry again and were about to strike again. After hearing about the situation, the manager immediately returned to the factory and sent someone to the union to request representatives to attend a consultation to resolve the issue. The union appointed representatives Chen Deheng, Hu Shaozhen, Qin Afa, and Lu Baohe to attend. They first asked the factory to immediately reinstate the six workers, including Chen A Da, who had been dismissed without cause, and then discuss all the conditions, so that the temporary strike could be avoided. Otherwise, the union would have no way to mediate. Manager Chen Zixin agreed in person to resign from his position as manager within a few days and act as a responsible mediator. The latest date for a satisfactory reply would be the 13th of this month. The union representatives believed that Chen Zixin seemed sincere and was an important figure in the Yangsi District Municipal Government, so there was hope for a satisfactory resolution. They were responsible for urging the workers to negotiate with the factory, endure a day or two, and wait for the factory to reply to the mediation, so that the labor unrest could be avoided from expanding. This was the most fortunate outcome. The storm subsided, and it was already past 10:00 PM. The representatives returned home and agreed to hold a joint meeting of the union the next morning to discuss the matter.

Memorial from the Pharmaceutical Workers' Union to the Civil Training Committee

Reasons for Repeatedly Presenting the Organization of a Trade Union

The Pharmaceutical Workers' Union submitted a document to the Civil Training Committee, stating: "We respectfully request that this be forwarded to the Central Government, consulted with the Executive Yuan of the National Government, and the Ministry of Industry to stop the National Pharmaceutical Trade Association from fabricating rumors and undermining our association. We also wish to clarify the legality of our association's organization. We have learned that in early June of this year, the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce submitted a document to the Central Government based on the request of the National Pharmaceutical Trade Association. The wording was absurd and insulting to our association. The entire document was intended to achieve the goal of dissolving our association and indulging their ambition to oppress workers. Therefore, they disregarded reason and treated the law as a mere formality. They also exaggerated their claims and engaged in rampant slander, accusing our association of being affiliated with the Communist Party, which is universally condemned throughout the country. They attempted to use cruel means to subject our association to unwarranted injustice and halt our activities. Their intentions are extremely sinister, but everyone knows what they are up to, how could they deceive the superiors who see everything clearly? Considering the history of our association, which has been evident since its establishment in the ninth year of the Republic, although it was once controlled by the General Labor Union, it was soon returned to the workers. (Omission) As for the claim that our association is not legally organized, workers of the same profession can legally organize a trade union, especially since it has been approved by the municipal party and government organs. How can it be said that the municipal party and government organs have also acted illegally? This principle is very clear and easily understood. The association's efforts are becoming increasingly clumsy and ridiculous. The work of our association members is divided and listed as follows: (1) Knife workers: specializing in slicing medicinal herbs, decocting tiger, deer, turtle, and donkey gelatin, etc. (2) Storage room workers: specializing in loading and unloading various slices, bringing them to the business counter, and sorting and selecting slices, etc. (3) General workers: specializing in all kinds of odd jobs such as washing, stir-frying, drying, packaging, calcining, and refining. (4) Raw material room workers: specializing in water-based honey pills, decocting pastes, etc. (5) Coarse goods room workers: specializing in the management of various raw materials. (6) Fine goods room workers: specializing in the management of all valuable goods and selecting raw materials. (7) Service workers: (A) Grinding room service workers: specializing in grinding various medicinal powders. (B) Warehouse service workers: specializing in carrying goods and all kinds of heavy odd jobs. (C) Kitchen service workers: specializing in kitchen management and food for the entire store. (8) Pill and powder workers: also responsible for hanging wax shells, mixing various fine materials into pills and powders, refining cinnabar powder, preparing eye medicine, and spreading plasters, etc. (9) Medicinal slice workers: also responsible for breaking Ophiopogon japonicus, splitting tangerine peel, cutting medicinal paper, and picking Tetrapanax papyrifer. (10) Gelatin factory workers: such as those at West Lake in Hangzhou, Huiquan in Wuxi, and the larger pharmacies in this city, all have gelatin factories in these locations. Every winter, workers are sent to the factories to decoct tiger, deer, turtle, donkey, and ejiao gelatin, etc. As mentioned above, the duties of workers in this industry are all technical and manual work, not direct service personnel. How can capital seek to destroy them? The actual situation is presented here, so it is self-evident whether this industry should be organized into a trade union. Therefore, we have prepared a document to submit to your committee, requesting that it be forwarded to the Central Government. If there is anything inappropriate, we ask that you review and implement it, which would be a great kindness. Respectfully submitted to the Public Training Committee of the Shanghai Special Municipal Executive Committee."
